WELL EVALUATION
Oasis Petroleum North America, LLC
Ruud 5493 43-23 8T2
Figure 1. Nabors 460 drilling Oasis Petroleum's Ruud 5493 43-23 8T2 well in September, 2014 located
approximately 15 miles northwest of New Town, in Mountrail County, North Dakota.
INTRODUCTION
The Oasis Petroleum North America, LLC Ruud 5493 43-23 8T2[SW SE Section 23,
T154N, R93W] is located approximately 15 miles northwest of New Town in Mountrail
County, ND. The Ruud 5493 43-23 8T2 is a horizontal second bench Three Forks well within
the Williston Basin consisting of one 9,515' lateral drilled toward the north. Geologically, the
Williston Basin is an intracratonic, structural, and sedimentary basin located at the western
edge of the Canadian Shield. Within the basin, the Three Forks Formation (Devonian)
consists of interbedded carbonate and clastic lithologies, which unconformably underlies the
Pronghorn Member of the Bakken Formation (formerly recognized as the Sanish Sand).
Advances in drilling and well stimulation have made the Three Forks Formation a viable oil
and gas resource.
OFFSET WELLS
Offset well data used for depth correlation during curve operations are found in the
`Structure' section appended to this report. The Ruud 5493 43-23 7T3, located 33 feet south
of the subject well, proved to be the most reliable and consistent of the primary offsets used
for depth correlation of formations above the Lodgepole and during the curve landing. Offset
well control was essential in curve operations, to successfully land within the second bench
target zone. Formation thicknesses expressed by gamma ray signatures in these wells were
compared to gamma data collected during drilling operations in order to successfully land the
curve. The target landing true vertical depth (TVD) was periodically updated to ensure
accurate landing of the curve.
ENGINEERING
The Ruud 5493 43-23 8T2 was re-entered on August 22, 2014 by Nabors 460. Drilling fluid
was diesel invert mud for the vertical and curve, and salt water mud for the lateral. Four trips
were made during the vertical. The first trip was one at 8,935' for a new bit due to slow
ROP. The second trip was at 9,365' to replace the motor. The bit and MWD tools were not
changed. The third trip was at 9,635' to replace the bit and the motor. This BHA was used
to reach the Kick off point at 10,223'. The last trip in the vertical was made to pick up the
curve assembly. The curve was drilled with an 8 ¾" PDC bit utilizing a 2.35° Cavari mud
motor. The curve required 27.5 hours and 809' of drilling and was landed at 11,033' MD
(10,691' TVD) with an inclination of 91.4°. Following the landing, 7" intermediate casing
was set and cemented to 11,003' MD. To start the lateral, a 6 Hughes PDC bit, MWD tool,
and a 1.5° fixed mud motor were used. This BHA drilled 5,200' in 114.5 hours to 16,233'
MD where the first trip in the lateral was made due to inability to control the tool face
resulting in ineffective slides. The bit was replaced with an identical Hughes PDC 6" bit.
This assembly drilled 4,314' in 68.5 hours to a TD of 20,547' MD. The BHA
accomplishments are tabulated in an appendix (BHA Record) to this report. The well reached
total depth (TD) at 20,547' MD at 0945 hrs CDT on September 9, 2014, generating an
exposure of 9,514 linear feet of 6 hole through the Three Forks target interval. The bottom
hole location (BHL) lies 9,910.56' north & 621.23' east of surface location or approximately
258.08' FNL and 1,063.77' FEL, NE NE Sec. 14, T154N, R93W.
GEOLOGY
Lithology
Sample logging began at 7,970' MD where the observed lithology consists of primarily shale
with thin interbedded sandstone units. The main zones of interest drilled at the subject well
include the Ratcliffe, Mission Canyon, Middle Member Bakken, and second bench interval
of the Three Forks formations.
The Ratcliffe interval of the Charles Formation
(Mississippian - Madison Group) was drilled at 8,949' TVD
(-6,607'), 3' High to the Ruud 5493 43-23 7T3. Samples from
the Ratcliffe range from a tan to light gray, medium brown,
microcrystalline limestone (Figure 2). Samples have no
visual porosity and no visible oil staining was observed. For
a more detailed hydrocarbon analysis, see `Gas and Oil
Shows' section below).
Figure 2. Cuttings of limestone from the Ratcliffe interval of the
Charles Formation.
The Mission Canyon Formation (Mississippian - Madison
Group) was drilled at 9,061' TVD (-6,719'), 4' high to the
Ruud 5493 43-23 7T3. Representative samples consist of a
tan light gray off white to brown microcrystalline limestone
(Figure 3). The samples did not contain any visual porosity
and no visible oil staining was observed.
Figure 3. Cuttings of limestone from the Mission Canyon Formation.
The Middle Member of the Bakken Formation (Late
Devonian-Early Mississippian) was drilled at 10,511' TVD
(-8,169'), 3' high to the Ruud 5493 43-23 7T3. Representative
samples consist of a light gray to off white tan, calcareous
silty sandstone with intergranular porosity and a trace light-
brown oil stain. (Figure 4). Strong hydrocarbon shows were
observed in this interval.
Figure 4. Cuttings of the Middle Bakken silty sandstone of the
Bakken Formation.
The second bench interval of the Three Forks Formation
(Late Devonian) was drilled at 10,671' TVD (-8,329'), 9' high
to the Ruud 5493 43-23 7T3. Representative samples consist
of pink to light brown and very light orange, crystalline
carbonate, sucrosic dolomite with intercrystalline porosity.
Interbedded with a gray green to pale light green shale with
trace-disseminated pyrite.
Figure 5. Cuttings of the argillaceous dolomite and crystalline
dolomite of the second bench interval Three Forks Formation.
Gas and Oil Shows
Hydrocarbon constituents (C1 through C4) are expressed in parts-per-million (ppm)
concentrations. Diesel-invert mud was used to drill the vertical and curve, while salt-water
mud was used to drill the lateral. During the vertical, gas shows ranged from 15-31 units
above a background of ~11 units against a 9.10-10.50 lb/gal diesel-invert mud weight.
Methane (C1) was observed throughout the vertical. Gases heavier than C1 were not
observed. After kicking off the curve, shows ranged from 30-68 units with background
ranging from 15-24 units. Shows remained low from kick-off through entry of the Upper
Bakken. Gas shows were elevated in respect to the vertical from this interval through the
entrance of the Three Forks Formation second bench. Shows from the Upper Bakken through
second Bench ranged from 35-137 units (C1) over a background of ~25 units against a diesel-
invert mud weight of 10.05 lb/gal. Upon drilling the second bench of the Three Forks to the
curve, landing back ground gas slowly started to taper down, before reverting to the low
magnitude previously observed in the vertical and early curve.
The lateral began with gas shows consistent with what was observed during the later part of
the curve landing. From ~ 13,200' - 13,250' MD background gas and shows briefly rose to 40
units (C1) over a background of 15-20 units against a 9.5 lb/gal salt-water mud weight.
Increased gas shows were observed frequently from ~13,700' - 14,100' ranging from 21-61
units (C1) over a background of 7-12 units against a 9.5 lb/gal salt-water mud weight.
Increased gas shows were again observed from ~14,400' - 14,600' ranging from 20-46 units
(C1) over a background of 10-14 units against a 9.5 lb/gal. salt-water mud weight. Gas levels
were elevated from ~14,700' - 15,000' with an average background of 25 units with shows as
high as 35 units (C1) against a 9.5 lb/gal salt-water mud weight. The magnitude of gas
increased again from ~15,700' ­ 16,750' with an average background of 35 units with shows
ranging from 39-74 units (C1-C2) against a 9.5 lb/gal salt-water mud weight. Elevated gas
levels were observed again from ~17,350' - 18,150' with an average background of 30 units
with shows as high as 69 units (C1) against a 9.5 lb/gal salt-water mud weight. Another
section of elevated gas levels were observed from ~18,550' - 19,350' with an average
background of 35 units with shows as high as 98 units (C1) against a 9.5 lb/gal salt-water
mud weight. From 19,350', the remainder of the well exhibited reduced gas levels ranging
from 17-51 units (C1) over a background of 10 units against a 9.5 lb/gal salt-water mud
weight.
GEOSTEERING
The potential pay zone of the Ruud 5493 43-23 8T2 was identified by evaluating electric log
data from the Mangum 5493 44-7 T3 (Figure 6).
Figure 6. Mangum 5493 44-7 T3 Type log. Ideal target zone highlighted in green.
The original prognosis had the curve landing at 10,700' TVD at 90.32°. The Base of Last Salt
top indicated that the target was approximately six feet high to the adjacent well Ruud 5493-
23 7T3. The decision was made to raise the target by five feet. The lower markers and
formation tops supported the decision to raise the target landing by additional 4 feet to
10,691' TVD. The wellbore was landed at a TVD of 10,691' at 91.4°, about 8' below the top
of the target zone in the second bench Three Forks target interval.
Drilling ahead out of the casing at a depth of 11,032' MD, the inclination remained high (90.5
- 91.9) for ~ 600 feet as the wellbore approached the top the zone. Frequent slides were
implemented during this interval to reduce the inclination; however, the wellbore also needed
to make a left turn to change the azimuth from ~30° to 0°. As a result, the inclination was
not reduced as much as needed. During this interval gamma gradually increased from ~ 110
to 170 api, with very erratic swings as much as 40 api throughout this section. As the
wellbore approached the upper boundary of the target zone the gamma fell to a low of 90 api.
Before reaching the top of the target zone, the inclination was reduced to a range of 87.9 ­
89.7 for ~ 300 feet. The high erratic gamma values were again observed indicative of the
mid to upper portion of the target zone. The wellbore reached the middle of the target zone
at ~ 12,000' MD.
From 12,000' MD to ~ 13,800' MD the wellbore gradually climbed toward the upper part of
the zone. The low gamma of 90 api was observed at ~12,600' and again at ~13,400' as the
wellbore peaked within 2 ­ 3 feet of the top of the target, which provided good markers for
calculating dip. At ~ 13,800' the wellbore began to climb sharply towards the upper target
zone. The slides were not effective enough to reduce the inclination and the wellbore crossed
above the upper target zone at ~14,000' and advanced to 3-4 feet above the zone before the
inclination was brought under control. Gamma above the target zone ranged from 120 ­ 150
api with erratic swings similar to the mid to upper portion of the target zone. The wellbore
crossed back into zone at ~14,400', providing good markers for calculating dip.
From 14,400' MD to ~15,000' MD the wellbore slowly dropped into the middle of the target
zone. From 15,000' MD to ~18,500' MD the wellbore remained in the middle of the target
zone, with one exception; when the wellbore approached the top of target ~16,200' MD due
to inability to control the tool face, at which point the BHA was replaced. The middle of the
zone was re-encountered at ~16,600' MD. A low gamma signature of 70 api was
encountered twice, a few feet below the mid point in the target zone, once at ~16,800' MD
and again at ~17,650 ' MD, both providing good markers for calculating dip. At ~18,500'
MD the inclination declined significantly causing the wellbore to dip below the target zone at
~19,000' MD and entering into the lower claystone at ~19,100' MD. No slides were
implemented while approaching the middle of the zone because the wellbore had a tendency
to build while rotating. In this case the wellbore dropped unexpectedly during rotation and it
was too late to recover before leaving zone. After implementing several slides, the wellbore
passed back into zone at ~19,950' MD. The wellbore returned to the middle of the target
zone before reaching TD. The dip profile is presented below in Figure 10.

SUMMARY
The Oasis Petroleum North America, LLC Ruud 5493 43-23 8T2 was drilled by Nabors
460 from reentry to TD in 19 days. The Ruud reached a total depth of 20,547' MD on
September 9, 2014. Geologic data, hydrocarbon gas measurements, and sample examination
obtained during the Ruud 5493 43-23 8T2 indicate hydrocarbon presence in the Three Forks
second bench Target. Samples from the target zone consist of light gray to off white, pink to
very light orange-red crystalline carbonate, microsucrosic dolomite with intercrystalline
porosity, which yielded very weak very slow pale yellow diffuse cut fluorescence. Lateral
operations were successful in exposing 9,515' of potentially productive Three Forks target
zone rock to the wellbore.
Respectfully submitted,
Alan Hardesty
Sunburst Consulting, Inc.
September 09, 2014

LITHOLOGY
Geologist caught lagged samples in 30' intervals under the supervision of
Sunburst geologists. 10' samples were taken under areas of increased scrutiny.
Sample or gamma ray marker tops have been inserted in the sample descriptions
below for reference. Samples were examined wet and dry under a binocular
microscope.
VERTICAL HOLE
Drilling in Kibbey Formation [Mississippian, Big Snowy Group]:
7,970-8,000
SILTSTONE: brown, dark red, friable, sub platy, calcareous cement, well cemented; trace
SANDSTONE: light gray-off white, very fine grained, firm, rounded, moderately cemented, no visible porosity, no
visible oil stain
8,000-8,030
SILTSTONE: brown, dark red, purple, friable, sub platy, calcareous cement, well cemented, sandy
in part; ANHYDRITE: microcrystalline, off white, soft, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
8,030-8,060
SILTSTONE: brown, dark red, purple, friable, sub platy, calcareous cement, well cemented, sandy
in part; ANHYDRITE: microcrystalline, off white, soft, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
8,060-8,090
SILTSTONE: brown, dark red, purple, friable, sub platy, calcareous cement, well cemented, sandy
in part; ANHYDRITE: microcrystalline, off white, soft, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
8,090-8,120
SILTSTONE: brown, dark red, light orange, friable, sub platy, calcareous cement, well cemented,
sandy in part; ANHYDRITE: microcrystalline, off white, soft, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
8,120-8,150
SILTSTONE: brown, dark red, light orange, friable, sub platy, calcareous cement, well cemented,
sandy in part, no visible porosity, no visible oil stain
Kibbey "Lime"
8,167' MD / 8,166' TVD (-5,824')
8,150-8,180

crystalline, firm, crystalline texture, very trace pinpoint porosity; ANHYDRITE: microcrystalline, off white, soft, no
visible porosity, no visible oil stain
8,180-8,210
LIMESTONE: mudstone, light gray, off white, very light brown, microcrystalline-very fine
crystalline, firm, crystalline texture, trace disseminated pyrite; ANHYDRITE: microcrystalline, off white, soft, no
visible porosity, no visible oil stain
8,210-8,240
SILTSTONE: light red, pink, firm, sub blocky, calcareous cement well cemented no visible
porosity, no visible oil stain
8,240-8,270
SILTSTONE: red to dark red, firm, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately cemented
8,270-8,300
SILTSTONE: red to dark red, firm, sub blocky, calcareous cement, moderately cemented

common SALT: clear to milky, hard

Well File # 28685
Dear Brandi:
Pursuant to Commission Order No. 23950, approval to drill the above captioned well is hereby given. The
approval is granted on the condition that all portions of the well bore not isolated by cement, be no closer than
the 200' setback from the north & south boundaries and 500' setback from the east & west boundaries within the
1280 acre spacing unit consisting of Sections 14 & 23 T154N R93W.
PERMIT STIPULATIONS: Effective June 1, 2014, a covered leak-proof container (with placard) for
filter sock disposal must be maintained on the well site beginning when the well is spud, and must
remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations are
conducted. Disposition of drill cuttings must be approved by the NDIC field inspector. OASIS PETRO
NO AMER must contact NDIC Field Inspector Jason Hicks at 701-720-3523 prior to location
construction.
Drilling pit
NDAC 43-02-03-19.4 states that "a pit may be utilized to bury drill cuttings and solids generated during well
drilling and completion operations, providing the pit can be constructed, used and reclaimed in a manner that will
prevent pollution of the land surface and freshwaters. Reserve and circulation of mud system through earthen pits
are prohibited. All pits shall be inspected by an authorized representative of the director prior to lining and use.
Drill cuttings and solids must be stabilized in a manner approved by the director prior to placement in a cuttings
pit."
Form 1 Changes & Hard Lines
Any changes, shortening of casing point or lengthening at Total Depth must have prior approval by the NDIC.
The proposed directional plan is at a legal location. Based on the azimuth of the proposed lateral the maximum
legal coordinate from the well head is: 9966' north.
Location Construction Commencement (Three Day Waiting Period)
Operators shall not commence operations on a drill site until the 3rd business day following publication of the
approved drilling permit on the NDIC - OGD Daily Activity Report. If circumstances require operations to
commence before the 3rd business day following publication on the Daily Activity Report, the waiting period may
be waived by the Director. Application for a waiver must be by sworn affidavit providing the information
necessary to evaluate the extenuating circumstances, the factors of NDAC 43-02-03-16.2 (1), (a)-(f), and any other
information that would allow the Director to conclude that in the event another owner seeks revocation of the
drilling permit, the applicant should retain the permit.
Brandi Terry
June 20, 2014
Page 2
Permit Fee & Notification
Payment was received in the amount of $100 via credit card .The permit fee has been received. It is requested
that notification be given immediately upon the spudding of the well. This information should be relayed to the
Oil & Gas Division, Bismarck, via telephone. The following information must be included: Well name, legal
location, permit number, drilling contractor, company representative, date and time of spudding. Office hours are
8:00 a.m. to 12:00 p.m. and 1:00 p.m. to 5:00 p.m. Central Time. Our telephone number is (701) 328-8020, leave a
message if after hours or on the weekend.
Survey Requirements for Horizontal, Horizontal Re-entry, and Directional Wells
NDAC Section 43-02-03-25 (Deviation Tests and Directional Surveys) states in part (that) the survey contractor
shall file a certified copy of all surveys with the director free of charge within thirty days of completion. Surveys
must be submitted as one electronic copy, or in a form approved by the director. However, the director may
require the directional survey to be filed immediately after completion if the survey is needed to conduct the
operation of the director's office in a timely manner. Certified surveys must be submitted via email in one adobe
document, with a certification cover page to certsurvey@nd.gov.
Survey points shall be of such frequency to accurately determine the entire location of the well bore.
Specifically, the Horizontal and Directional well survey frequency is 100 feet in the vertical, 30 feet in the curve
(or when sliding) and 90 feet in the lateral.
Surface casing cement
Tail cement utilized on surface casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi within 12
hours, and tail cement utilized on production casing must have a minimum compressive strength of 500 psi
before drilling the plug or initiating tests.
Logs NDAC Section 43-02-03-31 requires the running of (1) a suite of open hole logs from which formation tops and
porosity zones can be determined, (2) a Gamma Ray Log run from total depth to ground level elevation of the well bore, and
(3) a log from which the presence and quality of cement can be determined (Standard CBL or Ultrasonic cement evaluation
log) in every well in which production or intermediate casing has been set, this log must be run prior to completing the well.
All logs run must be submitted free of charge, as one digital TIFF (tagged image file format) copy and one digital LAS (log
ASCII) formatted copy. Digital logs may be submitted on a standard CD, DVD, or attached to an email sent to
digitallogs@nd.gov
Thank you for your cooperation.

Petroleum Resource Specialist
April 9, 2014
RE: Filter Socks and Other Filter Media
Leakproof Container Required
Oil and Gas Wells
Dear Operator,
North Dakota Administrative Code Section 43-02-03-19.2 states in part that all waste material associated with
exploration or production of oil and gas must be properly disposed of in an authorized facility in accord with all
applicable local, state, and federal laws and regulations.
Filtration systems are commonly used during oil and gas operations in North Dakota. The Commission is very
concerned about the proper disposal of used filters (including filter socks) used by the oil and gas industry.
Effective June 1, 2014, a container must be maintained on each well drilled in North Dakota beginning when the
well is spud and must remain on-site during clean-out, completion, and flow-back whenever filtration operations
are conducted. The on-site container must be used to store filters until they can be properly disposed of in an
authorized facility. Such containers must be:
leakproof to prevent any fluids from escaping the container
covered to prevent precipitation from entering the container
placard to indicate only filters are to be placed in the container
If the operator will not utilize a filtration system, a waiver to the container requirement will be considered, but
only upon the operator submitting a Sundry Notice (Form 4) justifying their request.
As previously stated in our March 13, 2014 letter, North Dakota Administrative Code Section 33-20-02.1-01
states in part that every person who transports solid waste (which includes oil and gas exploration and production
wastes) is required to have a valid permit issued by the North Dakota Department of Health, Division of Waste
Management. Please contact the Division of Waste Management at (701) 328-5166 with any questions on the
solid waste program. Note oil and gas exploration and production wastes include produced water, drilling mud,
invert mud, tank bottom sediment, pipe scale, filters, and fly ash.
Thank you for your cooperation.
Sincerely,
Bruce E. Hicks
Assistant Director
